## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.2 Response Surface Methodology:



### Subsection (optional): 12.2a Introduction to Response Surface Methodology



Response surface methodology (RSM) is a statistical approach used to explore the relationships between multiple explanatory variables and one or more response variables. It was first introduced by George E. P. Box and K. B. Wilson in 1951 and has since been widely used in various fields, including material selection and optimal design.



RSM is based on the idea of using a sequence of designed experiments to obtain an optimal response. This is achieved by fitting a second-degree polynomial model to the data, which allows for the identification of the most significant factors and interactions in a system. While this model is only an approximation, it is easy to estimate and apply, making it a practical choice for situations where little is known about the process.



## Practical Concerns



As with any statistical model, it is important to be aware that RSM is an approximation to reality. Both the models and the parameter values are subject to uncertainty and errors, which can affect the accuracy of the estimated optimum point. However, despite these limitations, RSM has a proven track record of helping researchers improve products and services.



One notable example is Box's original response-surface modeling, which enabled chemical engineers to improve a process that had been stuck at a saddle-point for years. By reducing the costs of experimentation, Box's design allowed for the fitting of a quadratic model, which led to a long-sought ascent direction.



## Advantages of Response Surface Methodology



One of the main advantages of using RSM is its ability to reduce the number of experimental runs required while still providing valuable information about the effects of input variables on the output response. This makes it a cost-effective and efficient tool for material selection and optimal design.



Additionally, RSM allows for the identification of the most significant factors and interactions in a system. By focusing on these factors, engineers can make more informed decisions and improve the overall performance of their products and services.



## Limitations of Response Surface Methodology



While RSM has many advantages, it also has some limitations that must be considered. One limitation is that it can only be used for systems with binary factors, meaning that each factor can only have two levels. This may not be suitable for all systems, and alternative experimental designs may need to be used.



Another limitation is that RSM is not suitable for systems with high-order interactions. As the resolution of the design decreases, the ability to separate main effects and low-order interactions from higher-order interactions also decreases. This means that RSM may not be suitable for systems with complex interactions.



## Conclusion



Response surface methodology is a powerful tool in the field of design of experiments, with applications in material selection and optimal design. While it has its limitations, its ability to reduce the number of experimental runs and identify significant factors and interactions makes it a valuable tool for engineers and researchers. By understanding the practical concerns and limitations of RSM, it can be used effectively to improve products and services.





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.2 Response Surface Methodology:



### Subsection (optional): 12.2b Application of Response Surface Methodology



Response surface methodology (RSM) is a powerful statistical tool that has been widely used in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. It allows researchers to explore the relationships between multiple explanatory variables and one or more response variables, and to identify the most significant factors and interactions in a system.



One of the main practical concerns when using RSM is the fact that it is an approximation to reality. Both the models and the parameter values are subject to uncertainty and errors, which can affect the accuracy of the estimated optimum point. However, despite these limitations, RSM has a proven track record of helping researchers improve products and services.



In material selection, RSM can be employed to optimize the production of a special substance by identifying the optimal combination of operational factors. This is achieved by using proper design of experiments (DoE) to reduce the number of experimental runs required while still providing valuable information about the effects of input variables.



For example, in the field of material science, RSM has been used to optimize the properties of composite materials by varying the composition and processing parameters. By using RSM, researchers were able to identify the optimal combination of factors that resulted in the desired properties, while minimizing the number of experimental runs required.



In optimal design, RSM has been used to improve the performance of products and services by identifying the optimal design parameters. This is achieved by fitting a second-degree polynomial model to the data, which allows for the identification of the most significant factors and interactions in a system. By using RSM, researchers can reduce the costs of experimentation and improve the overall performance of their designs.



One notable example of the successful application of RSM in optimal design is the case of Box's original response-surface modeling. By reducing the costs of experimentation, Box's design enabled chemical engineers to improve a process that had been stuck at a saddle-point for years. This led to a long-sought ascent direction, which greatly improved the performance of the process.



In conclusion, response surface methodology is a valuable tool for researchers in material selection and optimal design. Despite its limitations, RSM has a proven track record of helping researchers improve products and services by identifying the optimal combination of factors and interactions in a system. By using proper design of experiments and statistical models, RSM can greatly improve the efficiency and effectiveness of the design process.





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.2 Response Surface Methodology:



### Subsection (optional): 12.2c Advantages and Limitations of Response Surface Methodology



Response surface methodology (RSM) is a powerful statistical tool that has been widely used in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. It allows researchers to explore the relationships between multiple explanatory variables and one or more response variables, and to identify the most significant factors and interactions in a system.



One of the main practical concerns when using RSM is the fact that it is an approximation to reality. Both the models and the parameter values are subject to uncertainty and errors, which can affect the accuracy of the estimated optimum point. However, despite these limitations, RSM has a proven track record of helping researchers improve products and services.



In material selection, RSM can be employed to optimize the production of a special substance by identifying the optimal combination of operational factors. This is achieved by using proper design of experiments (DoE) to reduce the number of experimental runs required while still providing valuable information about the effects of input variables.



For example, in the field of material science, RSM has been used to optimize the properties of composite materials by varying the composition and processing parameters. By using RSM, researchers were able to identify the optimal combination of factors that resulted in the desired properties, while minimizing the number of experimental runs required.



In optimal design, RSM has been used to improve the performance of products and services by identifying the optimal design parameters. This is achieved by fitting a second-degree polynomial model to the data, which allows for the identification of the most significant factors and interactions. This approach has been successfully applied in various industries, such as manufacturing, engineering, and healthcare.



One of the main advantages of RSM is its ability to reduce the number of experimental runs required while still providing valuable information about the system. This is achieved by using proper DoE techniques, such as factorial designs, central composite designs, and Box-Behnken designs. These designs allow for the identification of the most significant factors and interactions, while minimizing the number of experimental runs required.



Another advantage of RSM is its flexibility in handling both continuous and categorical variables. This allows for a more comprehensive analysis of the system, as both types of variables can have an impact on the response. Additionally, RSM allows for the incorporation of constraints, such as upper and lower bounds, which can be useful in practical applications.



However, as with any statistical tool, RSM has its limitations. One of the main limitations is the assumption of a second-degree polynomial model. While this model is easy to estimate and apply, it may not accurately represent the true relationship between the variables and the response. This can lead to inaccurate predictions and suboptimal solutions.



Furthermore, RSM relies on the assumption of linearity and additivity of the effects of the variables. In reality, many systems exhibit non-linear and non-additive behavior, which can lead to inaccurate results. This limitation can be addressed by using higher-order models or by incorporating non-linear transformations of the variables.



In conclusion, response surface methodology is a powerful tool for optimizing systems and improving products and services. Its ability to reduce the number of experimental runs required while still providing valuable information makes it a valuable tool in material selection and optimal design. However, practitioners must be aware of its limitations and use it in conjunction with other techniques to ensure accurate and reliable results.





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.3 Box-Behnken Design:



### Subsection (optional): 12.3a Introduction to Box-Behnken Design



Box-Behnken design is a type of response surface methodology (RSM) that is commonly used in material selection and optimal design. It is a three-level factorial design that allows for the exploration of the relationships between multiple explanatory variables and one or more response variables. This design is particularly useful when the number of factors is large, as it reduces the number of experimental runs required while still providing valuable information about the effects of input variables.



Box-Behnken design is based on the concept of a central composite design (CCD), which is a type of response surface design that includes a central point and a set of star points. The central point is used to estimate the curvature of the response surface, while the star points are used to estimate the effects of the factors on the response variable. Box-Behnken design is a variation of CCD that uses a cube instead of a sphere to define the design space, resulting in a more efficient and balanced design.



One of the main advantages of Box-Behnken design is its ability to identify the most significant factors and interactions in a system. By using proper design of experiments (DoE), researchers can reduce the number of experimental runs required while still obtaining accurate estimates of the optimum point. This is particularly useful in material selection, where the production of a special substance can be optimized by identifying the optimal combination of operational factors.



For example, in the field of material science, Box-Behnken design has been used to optimize the properties of composite materials by varying the composition and processing parameters. By using this design, researchers were able to identify the optimal combination of factors that resulted in the desired properties, while minimizing the number of experimental runs required.



In optimal design, Box-Behnken design has been used to improve the performance of products and services by identifying the optimal design parameters. This is achieved by fitting a second-degree polynomial model to the data, which allows for the identification of the most significant factors and interactions. By using this design, researchers can efficiently explore the design space and identify the optimal design parameters that result in the desired performance.



In conclusion, Box-Behnken design is a powerful tool in the field of design of experiments, particularly in material selection and optimal design. Its ability to efficiently explore the design space and identify the most significant factors and interactions makes it a valuable tool for researchers looking to improve products and services. 





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.3 Box-Behnken Design:



### Subsection (optional): 12.3b Application of Box-Behnken Design



Box-Behnken design has been widely used in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In this section, we will explore some specific applications of this design in different industries.



#### Application in Material Science



One of the most common applications of Box-Behnken design is in material science. This design has been used to optimize the properties of composite materials by varying the composition and processing parameters. For example, researchers have used this design to study the effects of different filler materials and processing conditions on the mechanical properties of polymer composites. By varying the levels of these factors, they were able to identify the optimal combination that resulted in the highest strength and stiffness.



Another application of Box-Behnken design in material science is in the development of new alloys. By varying the composition and processing parameters, researchers can identify the optimal combination that results in the desired properties, such as corrosion resistance, strength, and ductility. This approach has been used to develop new high-strength aluminum alloys for use in the aerospace industry.



#### Application in Chemical Engineering



Box-Behnken design has also been widely used in chemical engineering for process optimization. In this field, the design is used to identify the optimal combination of operational factors that result in the desired product quality and yield. For example, in the production of pharmaceuticals, researchers have used this design to optimize the reaction conditions, such as temperature, pressure, and reactant concentrations, to achieve the highest purity and yield.



#### Application in Manufacturing



In the manufacturing industry, Box-Behnken design has been used to optimize the production process and reduce costs. For instance, in the production of electronic devices, this design has been used to identify the optimal combination of process parameters, such as temperature, pressure, and time, to achieve the desired product quality while minimizing production time and costs.



#### Application in Quality Control



Box-Behnken design has also been used in quality control to identify the factors that have the most significant impact on product quality. By varying the levels of these factors, researchers can determine the optimal combination that results in the highest quality product. This approach has been used in various industries, such as food and beverage, to ensure consistent product quality and reduce waste.



In conclusion, Box-Behnken design has a wide range of applications in different industries, making it a valuable tool for material selection and optimal design. By using this design, researchers can efficiently identify the most significant factors and interactions in a system, leading to improved product quality, reduced costs, and increased efficiency. 





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.3 Box-Behnken Design:



### Subsection (optional): 12.3c Advantages and Limitations of Box-Behnken Design



Box-Behnken design is a popular and widely used experimental design method that offers several advantages over other designs. However, like any other method, it also has its limitations. In this section, we will discuss the advantages and limitations of Box-Behnken design in detail.



#### Advantages of Box-Behnken Design



1. Reduced number of experiments: One of the main advantages of Box-Behnken design is that it requires a smaller number of experiments compared to other designs, such as full factorial design. This is because Box-Behnken design uses a combination of full and fractional factorial designs, which allows for a more efficient use of resources.



2. Efficient identification of optimal conditions: Box-Behnken design is specifically designed to identify the optimal conditions for a process or product. By varying the levels of factors within a predetermined range, this design allows for the efficient identification of the optimal combination that results in the desired outcome.



3. Reduced time and cost: Due to the reduced number of experiments, Box-Behnken design can save both time and cost in the experimental process. This makes it a more practical and feasible option for industries and researchers with limited resources.



4. Ability to study curvature: Unlike other designs, Box-Behnken design allows for the study of curvature in the response surface. This means that it can capture non-linear relationships between factors and responses, which is often the case in real-world scenarios.



#### Limitations of Box-Behnken Design



1. Limited number of factors: Box-Behnken design is not suitable for experiments with a large number of factors. This is because the number of experiments increases exponentially with the number of factors, making it impractical for designs with more than 5 or 6 factors.



2. Limited range of factor levels: Box-Behnken design requires the factors to be set at three levels, which may not always be feasible or practical. This limitation can restrict the applicability of this design in certain scenarios.



3. Inability to detect interactions: Box-Behnken design is not suitable for studying interactions between factors. This is because it uses a fractional factorial design, which does not allow for the estimation of interaction effects.



4. Sensitivity to outliers: Box-Behnken design is sensitive to outliers, which can significantly affect the results and lead to incorrect conclusions. This makes it important to carefully analyze and validate the data before drawing any conclusions.



In conclusion, Box-Behnken design offers several advantages over other experimental designs, such as reduced number of experiments and efficient identification of optimal conditions. However, it also has its limitations, such as the limited number of factors and inability to detect interactions. Therefore, it is important to carefully consider the specific requirements of the experiment before choosing Box-Behnken design as the experimental method.





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.4 Central Composite Design:



### Subsection (optional): 12.4a Introduction to Central Composite Design



Central Composite Design (CCD) is a popular and versatile experimental design method that is widely used in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. It is a type of response surface methodology (RSM) that allows for the efficient exploration of the relationship between factors and responses. In this section, we will discuss the basics of CCD and its applications in material selection and optimal design.



#### Basics of Central Composite Design



CCD is a three-stage design that combines full and fractional factorial designs with center points to create a response surface. The design consists of three types of points: factorial points, axial points, and center points. Factorial points are used to estimate the main effects of factors, axial points are used to estimate the quadratic effects, and center points are used to estimate the pure error. The number of points in each category depends on the number of factors and the desired level of precision.



The design is typically represented in a cube or a sphere, with the factorial points located at the corners, the axial points at the midpoints of the edges, and the center points at the center. The distance between the center points and the factorial points is known as the alpha distance, and it determines the level of precision in estimating the quadratic effects.



#### Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design



CCD is a powerful tool for material selection and optimal design due to its ability to efficiently explore the relationship between factors and responses. It allows for the identification of the optimal combination of factors that results in the desired response, while also providing information about the curvature of the response surface.



In material selection, CCD can be used to study the effects of various material properties on the performance of a product. By varying the levels of factors such as strength, stiffness, and density, CCD can help identify the optimal combination of material properties that results in the desired performance.



In optimal design, CCD can be used to study the effects of design parameters on the performance of a product. By varying the levels of factors such as dimensions, shape, and material thickness, CCD can help identify the optimal design that results in the desired performance.



#### Conclusion



In conclusion, CCD is a powerful and versatile experimental design method that is widely used in material selection and optimal design. Its ability to efficiently explore the relationship between factors and responses makes it a valuable tool for industries and researchers with limited resources. In the next section, we will discuss the advantages and limitations of CCD in more detail.

### Subsection (optional): 12.4b Application of Central Composite Design



Central Composite Design (CCD) is a powerful tool that has been widely used in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In this section, we will discuss some specific applications of CCD in these areas.



#### Material Selection



Material selection is a critical aspect of product design, as it directly affects the performance, cost, and sustainability of a product. CCD can be used to efficiently explore the relationship between material properties and product performance. By varying the levels of different material properties, such as strength, density, and thermal conductivity, CCD can identify the optimal combination of properties that results in the desired product performance.



For example, in the design of a lightweight and durable bicycle frame, CCD can be used to determine the optimal combination of material properties, such as tensile strength, Young's modulus, and density, to achieve the desired balance of strength and weight. This can lead to a more efficient and cost-effective design, as well as a more sustainable product.



#### Optimal Design



Optimal design involves finding the best combination of design parameters to achieve a desired performance or outcome. CCD can be used to efficiently explore the relationship between design parameters and product performance, allowing for the identification of the optimal design.



For instance, in the design of a heat exchanger, CCD can be used to determine the optimal combination of design parameters, such as tube diameter, tube length, and fluid flow rate, to achieve the desired heat transfer rate. This can lead to a more efficient and cost-effective design, as well as a more sustainable product.



#### Other Applications



In addition to material selection and optimal design, CCD has been applied in various other areas, such as process optimization, quality control, and reliability analysis. For example, in process optimization, CCD can be used to identify the optimal combination of process parameters to achieve the desired product quality. In quality control, CCD can be used to determine the optimal levels of different factors to minimize variability and defects in a product. In reliability analysis, CCD can be used to identify the optimal combination of design parameters to maximize the reliability and lifespan of a product.



#### Conclusion



In conclusion, CCD is a versatile and powerful tool that has numerous applications in material selection and optimal design. Its ability to efficiently explore the relationship between factors and responses makes it a valuable tool for engineers and researchers in various fields. By using CCD, we can achieve more efficient, cost-effective, and sustainable designs, leading to better products and processes. 





# MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide":



## Chapter: - Chapter 12: Advanced Topics in Design of Experiments:



### Section: - Section: 12.4 Central Composite Design:



### Subsection (optional): 12.4c Advantages and Limitations of Central Composite Design



Central Composite Design (CCD) is a widely used experimental design technique that allows for efficient exploration of the relationship between input variables and output responses. It is a type of response surface methodology (RSM) that is particularly useful in material selection and optimal design. In this section, we will discuss the advantages and limitations of CCD in these areas.



#### Advantages of Central Composite Design



1. Efficient exploration of the design space: CCD allows for the efficient exploration of the design space by using a relatively small number of experimental runs. This is achieved by combining the principles of factorial design and rotatable design, which allows for the estimation of both linear and quadratic effects of the input variables.



2. Flexibility in experimental design: CCD offers flexibility in experimental design by allowing for the inclusion of categorical and continuous variables, as well as the ability to vary the levels of these variables. This makes it suitable for a wide range of applications, including material selection and optimal design.



3. Ability to model curvature: CCD is able to model curvature in the response surface, which is important in cases where the relationship between input variables and output responses is not linear. This allows for a more accurate representation of the true relationship between the variables.



4. Robustness to noise: CCD is robust to noise in the experimental data, which is important in real-world applications where there may be variability in the data due to factors such as measurement error or environmental conditions.



#### Limitations of Central Composite Design



1. Limited to second-order models: CCD is limited to second-order models, which means that it can only capture linear and quadratic effects of the input variables. This may not be sufficient in cases where higher-order effects are present.



2. Requires a large number of runs for higher dimensions: As the number of input variables increases, the number of experimental runs required for CCD also increases. This can become impractical for higher dimensions, making it less suitable for complex systems.



3. Assumes a spherical design space: CCD assumes a spherical design space, which may not be applicable in all cases. This can lead to inaccurate results if the design space is not spherical.



4. Limited to continuous variables: CCD is limited to continuous variables, which means that it cannot handle categorical variables. This may be a limitation in certain applications where categorical variables play a significant role.



In conclusion, Central Composite Design offers many advantages in material selection and optimal design, such as efficient exploration of the design space and flexibility in experimental design. However, it also has some limitations, such as being limited to second-order models and continuous variables. It is important to carefully consider these advantages and limitations when deciding whether to use CCD in a particular application.

We have also looked at the application of MADM in optimal design, where it can aid in finding the optimal combination of design variables to achieve the desired performance.



We began by discussing the basics of MADM, including the different types of MADM methods and their advantages and limitations. We then delved into more advanced topics, such as the use of fuzzy logic in MADM and the incorporation of uncertainty in decision-making. Furthermore, we discussed the importance of experimental design in MADM and how it can help in reducing the number of experiments needed to obtain reliable results. We looked at different types of experimental designs, such as factorial designs and response surface methodology, and their applications in MADM. Overall, this chapter has provided a comprehensive guide to the use of MADM in material selection and optimal design. By understanding the principles and applications of MADM, engineers and researchers can make more informed decisions and achieve better results in their design processes.

## Chapter: MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide



### Introduction



In the previous chapters, we have covered the fundamentals of Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) and its applications in material selection and optimal design. We have explored various MADM methods such as the Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP), Technique for Order of Preference by Similarity to Ideal Solution (TOPSIS), and Preference Ranking Organization Method for Enrichment Evaluation (PROMETHEE). We have also discussed how these methods can be used to make decisions in material selection and optimal design problems.



In this chapter, we will delve into advanced topics in case studies using MADM. We will explore real-world examples and case studies where MADM has been successfully applied in material selection and optimal design. These case studies will provide a deeper understanding of how MADM can be used in practical situations and its effectiveness in decision-making.



We will also discuss the limitations and challenges of using MADM in case studies. This will help readers understand the potential pitfalls and how to overcome them when applying MADM in their own projects.



Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide on advanced topics in case studies using MADM. It will serve as a valuable resource for engineers, researchers, and students who are interested in using MADM for material selection and optimal design. 





### Section: 13.1 Case Study: Material Selection for Renewable Energy Applications:



Renewable energy is becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable energy sources. However, the materials used in renewable energy applications must also be carefully selected to ensure optimal performance and longevity. In this section, we will explore a case study on material selection for renewable energy applications, specifically focusing on thermal energy storage for solar thermal power plants.



#### 13.1a Introduction to Material Selection for Renewable Energy Applications



As mentioned in the previous section, thermal energy storage is crucial for solar thermal power plants to produce electricity at night and on overcast days. This allows for the use of solar power for baseload generation, reducing the reliance on traditional fossil fuel sources. However, the selection of materials for thermal energy storage is critical for the overall efficiency and cost-effectiveness of the power plant.



One of the main challenges in material selection for thermal energy storage is finding a material that can withstand high temperatures and thermal cycling without degrading. This is especially important for solar thermal power plants, where the storage medium is constantly exposed to high temperatures during the day and then cooled down at night.



In the past, pressurized steam and molten salt have been commonly used as thermal storage media. However, these materials have their limitations, such as high costs and potential corrosion issues. Therefore, there is a need for alternative materials that can provide efficient and cost-effective thermal energy storage.



To address this challenge, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different materials for thermal energy storage in a solar thermal power plant. The materials considered were concrete, phase change materials, and molten salts such as calcium, sodium, and potassium nitrate.



The case study used the Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP) method to evaluate the materials based on various criteria, including thermal stability, cost, and availability. The results showed that phase change materials, specifically paraffin wax, were the most suitable material for thermal energy storage in solar thermal power plants. Paraffin wax has a high latent heat capacity, making it an efficient storage medium, and it is also readily available and cost-effective.



This case study highlights the importance of using MADM methods in material selection for renewable energy applications. By considering multiple criteria and using a systematic approach, engineers can make informed decisions on the most suitable materials for thermal energy storage, ultimately improving the efficiency and sustainability of solar thermal power plants. 





### Section: 13.1 Case Study: Material Selection for Renewable Energy Applications:



Renewable energy is becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable energy sources. However, the materials used in renewable energy applications must also be carefully selected to ensure optimal performance and longevity. In this section, we will explore a case study on material selection for renewable energy applications, specifically focusing on thermal energy storage for solar thermal power plants.



#### 13.1a Introduction to Material Selection for Renewable Energy Applications



As mentioned in the previous section, thermal energy storage is crucial for solar thermal power plants to produce electricity at night and on overcast days. This allows for the use of solar power for baseload generation, reducing the reliance on traditional fossil fuel sources. However, the selection of materials for thermal energy storage is critical for the overall efficiency and cost-effectiveness of the power plant.



One of the main challenges in material selection for thermal energy storage is finding a material that can withstand high temperatures and thermal cycling without degrading. This is especially important for solar thermal power plants, where the storage medium is constantly exposed to high temperatures during the day and then cooled down at night.



In the past, pressurized steam and molten salt have been commonly used as thermal storage media. However, these materials have their limitations, such as high costs and potential corrosion issues. Therefore, there is a need for alternative materials that can provide efficient and cost-effective thermal energy storage.



To address this challenge, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different materials for thermal energy storage in a solar thermal power plant. The materials considered were concrete, phase change materials, and molten salts such as calcium, sodium, and potassium nitrate.



The case study utilized the MADM (Multi-Attribute Decision Making) method to evaluate and compare the materials based on multiple criteria, including thermal stability, cost, and environmental impact. MADM is a decision-making tool that allows for the consideration of multiple criteria and their relative importance in decision making. It is commonly used in engineering and management fields to make complex decisions involving multiple factors.



The results of the case study showed that phase change materials, specifically paraffin wax, were the most suitable material for thermal energy storage in solar thermal power plants. Paraffin wax has a high latent heat capacity, allowing it to store more thermal energy per unit mass compared to other materials. It also has a low cost and is environmentally friendly, making it a highly desirable option for renewable energy applications.



In conclusion, the application of MADM in material selection for renewable energy applications can provide valuable insights and aid in making informed decisions. It allows for a comprehensive evaluation of materials based on multiple criteria, leading to the selection of the most suitable material for a specific application. As renewable energy continues to play a crucial role in our energy mix, the use of MADM in material selection will become increasingly important in ensuring the efficiency and sustainability of renewable energy systems.





### Section: 13.1 Case Study: Material Selection for Renewable Energy Applications:



Renewable energy is becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable energy sources. However, the materials used in renewable energy applications must also be carefully selected to ensure optimal performance and longevity. In this section, we will explore a case study on material selection for renewable energy applications, specifically focusing on thermal energy storage for solar thermal power plants.



#### 13.1a Introduction to Material Selection for Renewable Energy Applications



As mentioned in the previous section, thermal energy storage is crucial for solar thermal power plants to produce electricity at night and on overcast days. This allows for the use of solar power for baseload generation, reducing the reliance on traditional fossil fuel sources. However, the selection of materials for thermal energy storage is critical for the overall efficiency and cost-effectiveness of the power plant.



One of the main challenges in material selection for thermal energy storage is finding a material that can withstand high temperatures and thermal cycling without degrading. This is especially important for solar thermal power plants, where the storage medium is constantly exposed to high temperatures during the day and then cooled down at night.



In the past, pressurized steam and molten salt have been commonly used as thermal storage media. However, these materials have their limitations, such as high costs and potential corrosion issues. Therefore, there is a need for alternative materials that can provide efficient and cost-effective thermal energy storage.



To address this challenge, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different materials for thermal energy storage in a solar thermal power plant. The materials considered were concrete, phase change materials, and molten salts such as calcium, sodium, and potassium nitrate.



The case study focused on a solar thermal power plant located in a desert region with high solar irradiance. The plant had a capacity of 100 MW and used a parabolic trough system to collect and concentrate solar energy. The thermal energy storage system was designed to store enough energy to generate electricity for 6 hours after sunset.



The performance of each material was evaluated based on their thermal properties, cost, and durability. Concrete was found to have a low cost but a low thermal conductivity, making it less efficient for thermal energy storage. Phase change materials, on the other hand, had a high thermal conductivity but were more expensive. Molten salts were found to have a good balance of thermal properties and cost, but their corrosive nature posed a potential issue.



After considering all factors, it was determined that molten salts, specifically a eutectic mixture of sodium and potassium nitrate, were the most suitable material for thermal energy storage in this case. They had a high thermal conductivity, low cost, and were able to withstand the high temperatures and thermal cycling without significant degradation.



The case study also explored the use of advanced materials, such as graphene and carbon nanotubes, for thermal energy storage. While these materials showed promising results in terms of thermal properties, their high cost and limited availability made them less feasible for large-scale applications.



In conclusion, material selection for renewable energy applications, specifically thermal energy storage, is a crucial aspect that must be carefully considered. The case study highlighted the importance of evaluating multiple factors, such as thermal properties, cost, and durability, to determine the most suitable material for a specific application. As renewable energy continues to play a larger role in our energy mix, further research and development in advanced materials may lead to even more efficient and cost-effective solutions for thermal energy storage.





### Section: 13.2 Case Study: Optimal Design of Renewable Energy Systems:



Renewable energy systems are becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable energy sources. However, the design of these systems must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on the optimal design of renewable energy systems, specifically focusing on the integration of different renewable energy sources.



#### 13.2a Introduction to Optimal Design of Renewable Energy Systems



As mentioned in the previous section, renewable energy systems often consist of multiple energy sources, such as solar, wind, and hydro power. The optimal design of these systems involves finding the most efficient and cost-effective way to integrate these different sources to meet the energy demand.



One approach to optimizing the design of renewable energy systems is through the use of Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods. MADM is a mathematical approach that allows for the comparison of multiple alternatives based on multiple criteria. This method has been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design.



To demonstrate the application of MADM in renewable energy systems, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different design options for a renewable energy system. The design options considered were a standalone solar system, a standalone wind system, and a hybrid system that combines both solar and wind energy.



The criteria used for comparison were the levelized cost of energy (LCOE), the reliability of the system, and the environmental impact. The LCOE is a measure of the cost of electricity generated by the system, while the reliability and environmental impact are important factors in the overall sustainability of the system.



Using MADM methods, the optimal design option was determined to be the hybrid system, which had the lowest LCOE, high reliability, and a relatively low environmental impact. This case study highlights the effectiveness of MADM in optimizing the design of renewable energy systems.



In the next section, we will explore another case study that focuses on the material selection for a specific renewable energy application.





### Section: 13.2 Case Study: Optimal Design of Renewable Energy Systems:



Renewable energy systems are becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable energy sources. However, the design of these systems must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on the optimal design of renewable energy systems, specifically focusing on the integration of different renewable energy sources.



#### 13.2a Introduction to Optimal Design of Renewable Energy Systems



As mentioned in the previous section, renewable energy systems often consist of multiple energy sources, such as solar, wind, and hydro power. The optimal design of these systems involves finding the most efficient and cost-effective way to integrate these different sources to meet the energy demand.



One approach to optimizing the design of renewable energy systems is through the use of Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods. MADM is a mathematical approach that allows for the comparison of multiple alternatives based on multiple criteria. This method has been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design.



To demonstrate the application of MADM in renewable energy systems, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different design options for a renewable energy system. The design options considered were a standalone solar system, a standalone wind system, and a hybrid system that combines both solar and wind energy.



The criteria used for comparison were the levelized cost of energy (LCOE), the reliability of the system, and the environmental impact. The LCOE is a measure of the cost of electricity generated by the system, while the reliability and environmental impact are important factors in the overall sustainability of the system.



Using MADM methods, the optimal design option was determined to be the hybrid system, which had the lowest LCOE, high reliability, and minimal environmental impact. This result highlights the effectiveness of MADM in finding the most suitable design option for renewable energy systems.



#### 13.2b Application of Optimal Design Techniques in Renewable Energy Systems



In addition to MADM, there are other optimal design techniques that can be applied in renewable energy systems. One such technique is the use of linear programming models, such as URBS (Urban Renewable Energy System) and SIREN (SEN Integrated Renewable Energy Network Toolkit).



URBS, developed by the Technical University of Munich, is a linear programming model that explores capacity expansion and unit commitment problems in distributed energy systems. It uses a time resolution of one hour and decision variables such as capacities for production, storage, and transport of electricity. URBS has been used to explore cost-optimal extensions to the European transmission grid and energy systems spanning Europe, the Middle East, and North Africa.



SIREN, developed by Sustainable Energy Now, is another linear programming model that uses the System Advisor Model (SAM) from the US National Renewable Energy Laboratory to perform energy calculations. It uses hourly datasets to model a given geographic region and allows users to explore the location and scale of renewable energy systems.



These optimal design techniques can be applied in renewable energy systems to find the most efficient and cost-effective design options. By considering multiple criteria and using mathematical models, these techniques can help in the decision-making process for renewable energy systems. 





### Section: 13.2 Case Study: Optimal Design of Renewable Energy Systems:



Renewable energy systems are becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable energy sources. However, the design of these systems must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on the optimal design of renewable energy systems, specifically focusing on the integration of different renewable energy sources.



#### 13.2c Case Study: Renewable Energy System Design



In recent years, there has been a growing interest in the development and implementation of renewable energy systems. These systems offer a sustainable and environmentally friendly alternative to traditional energy sources, such as fossil fuels. However, the design of these systems is crucial in order to maximize their efficiency and cost-effectiveness.



One approach to optimizing the design of renewable energy systems is through the use of Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods. MADM is a mathematical approach that allows for the comparison of multiple alternatives based on multiple criteria. This method has been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design.



To demonstrate the application of MADM in renewable energy systems, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different design options for a renewable energy system. The design options considered were a standalone solar system, a standalone wind system, and a hybrid system that combines both solar and wind energy.



The criteria used for comparison were the levelized cost of energy (LCOE), the reliability of the system, and the environmental impact. The LCOE is a measure of the cost of electricity generated by the system, while the reliability and environmental impact are important factors in the overall sustainability of the system.



Using MADM methods, the optimal design option was determined to be the hybrid system, which had the lowest LCOE, high reliability, and minimal environmental impact. This result highlights the importance of considering multiple criteria in the design of renewable energy systems.



One tool that has been used in the optimization of renewable energy systems is the SEN Integrated Renewable Energy Network Toolkit (SIREN). This software utilizes open or publicly available data sources to model a given geographic region and explore the location and scale of renewable energy sources to meet a specified electricity demand. SIREN has been used in a 2016 study to analyze Western Australia's South-West Interconnected System (SWIS) and found that it can transition to 85% renewable energy for the same cost as new coal and gas, with a significant reduction in emissions.



Another tool that has been developed for the optimization of renewable energy systems is the Solar, Wind, Conventional, and Hydroelectric Generation and Transmission (SWITCH) model. This model, developed by the Department of Electrical Engineering at the University of Hawaiʻi at Mānoa, uses optimization techniques to identify the most cost-effective generator and transmission projects for a power system with large shares of renewable energy.



In conclusion, the optimal design of renewable energy systems is a complex and important task that requires the consideration of multiple criteria. MADM methods, along with tools such as SIREN and SWITCH, can aid in this process and help to create sustainable and efficient renewable energy systems. 





### Section: 13.3 Case Study: Material Selection for Biodegradable Products:



Biodegradable products are becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable and environmentally friendly alternatives. However, the selection of materials for these products must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on material selection for biodegradable products using Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods.



#### 13.3a Introduction to Material Selection for Biodegradable Products



The use of biodegradable materials in products has gained significant attention in recent years due to their potential to reduce environmental impact. These materials can be broken down by natural processes, such as bacteria and fungi, into simpler substances, reducing the amount of waste in landfills and oceans. However, the selection of materials for biodegradable products is not a straightforward process, as there are various factors that must be considered.



One of the main challenges in material selection for biodegradable products is finding a balance between cost and properties. As mentioned in the previous section, the cost of materials plays a significant role in their selection. However, for biodegradable products, other factors such as biodegradability, mechanical properties, and environmental impact must also be taken into account.



MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different materials based on multiple criteria. These methods have been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In the following case study, we will use MADM methods to compare and select the optimal material for a biodegradable product.



#### 13.3b Case Study: Material Selection for Biodegradable Cutlery



To demonstrate the application of MADM in material selection for biodegradable products, a case study was conducted to compare the performance of different materials for biodegradable cutlery. The materials considered were polylactic acid (PLA), polyhydroxyalkanoates (PHA), and starch-based bioplastics.



The criteria used for comparison were biodegradability, mechanical properties, and cost. Biodegradability was measured by the time it takes for the material to completely degrade in a composting environment. Mechanical properties, such as strength and stiffness, were evaluated to ensure the cutlery could perform its intended function. Cost was also considered, as it is a crucial factor in the commercial viability of the product.



Using MADM methods, the optimal material for biodegradable cutlery was determined to be PLA. PLA had the shortest biodegradation time, comparable mechanical properties to PHA, and a lower cost compared to both PHA and starch-based bioplastics. This case study highlights the importance of considering multiple criteria in material selection for biodegradable products and the effectiveness of MADM methods in making informed decisions.



In conclusion, material selection for biodegradable products requires a careful evaluation of various factors, including cost, properties, and environmental impact. MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different materials, making them a valuable tool in the design and development of sustainable products. 





### Section: 13.3 Case Study: Material Selection for Biodegradable Products:



Biodegradable products are becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable and environmentally friendly alternatives. However, the selection of materials for these products must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on material selection for biodegradable products using Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods.



#### 13.3a Introduction to Material Selection for Biodegradable Products



The use of biodegradable materials in products has gained significant attention in recent years due to their potential to reduce environmental impact. These materials can be broken down by natural processes, such as bacteria and fungi, into simpler substances, reducing the amount of waste in landfills and oceans. However, the selection of materials for biodegradable products is not a straightforward process, as there are various factors that must be considered.



One of the main challenges in material selection for biodegradable products is finding a balance between cost and properties. As mentioned in the previous section, the cost of materials plays a significant role in their selection. However, for biodegradable products, other factors such as biodegradability, mechanical properties, and environmental impact must also be taken into account.



MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different materials based on multiple criteria. These methods have been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In the following case study, we will use MADM methods to compare and select the optimal material for a biodegradable product.



#### 13.3b Application of MADM in Biodegradable Product Material Selection



To demonstrate the application of MADM in material selection for biodegradable products, a case study was conducted to compare and select the optimal material for biodegradable cutlery. The criteria for material selection were biodegradability, mechanical properties, and cost. The materials considered were polylactic acid (PLA), polyhydroxyalkanoates (PHA), and starch-based bioplastics.



First, the biodegradability of each material was evaluated using the ASTM D6400 standard, which measures the rate of biodegradation in a controlled composting environment. PLA and PHA were found to have a higher biodegradability rate compared to starch-based bioplastics. Next, the mechanical properties of each material were compared, including tensile strength, impact strength, and flexibility. PLA and PHA were found to have superior mechanical properties compared to starch-based bioplastics.



Finally, the cost of each material was evaluated, taking into account the cost of production, processing, and disposal. PLA was found to be the most expensive material, followed by PHA and starch-based bioplastics. However, when considering the environmental impact of each material, PLA and PHA were found to have a lower carbon footprint compared to starch-based bioplastics.



Using the MADM method, a weighted decision matrix was created to compare the materials based on the three criteria. The weights were assigned based on the importance of each criterion, with biodegradability and mechanical properties having a higher weight compared to cost. After evaluating each material, PLA was found to be the optimal choice for biodegradable cutlery due to its high biodegradability rate and superior mechanical properties, despite its higher cost.



In conclusion, the application of MADM methods in material selection for biodegradable products can help identify the optimal material that balances cost, properties, and environmental impact. This approach can aid in the development of more sustainable and environmentally friendly products, contributing to a greener future.





### Section: 13.3 Case Study: Material Selection for Biodegradable Products:



Biodegradable products are becoming increasingly important as the world shifts towards more sustainable and environmentally friendly alternatives. However, the selection of materials for these products must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on material selection for biodegradable products using Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods.



#### 13.3a Introduction to Material Selection for Biodegradable Products



The use of biodegradable materials in products has gained significant attention in recent years due to their potential to reduce environmental impact. These materials can be broken down by natural processes, such as bacteria and fungi, into simpler substances, reducing the amount of waste in landfills and oceans. However, the selection of materials for biodegradable products is not a straightforward process, as there are various factors that must be considered.



One of the main challenges in material selection for biodegradable products is finding a balance between cost and properties. As mentioned in the previous section, the cost of materials plays a significant role in their selection. However, for biodegradable products, other factors such as biodegradability, mechanical properties, and environmental impact must also be taken into account.



MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different materials based on multiple criteria. These methods have been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In the following case study, we will use MADM methods to compare and select the optimal material for a biodegradable product.



#### 13.3b Application of MADM in Biodegradable Product Material Selection



To demonstrate the application of MADM in material selection for biodegradable products, a case study was conducted to select the optimal material for a biodegradable water bottle. The criteria for material selection were biodegradability, mechanical properties, cost, and environmental impact. The materials considered were PLA (polylactic acid), PHA (polyhydroxyalkanoates), and PBAT (polybutylene adipate terephthalate).



To evaluate the materials, the Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP) method was used. AHP is a widely used MADM method that allows for the comparison of alternatives based on multiple criteria. The process involves breaking down the main decision into a hierarchy of criteria and sub-criteria, assigning weights to each criterion, and then comparing alternatives based on each criterion.



The results of the AHP analysis showed that PLA was the optimal material for the biodegradable water bottle, with a weight of 0.47. PHA and PBAT had weights of 0.31 and 0.22, respectively. This decision was based on the fact that PLA had the highest biodegradability and mechanical properties, while also being relatively cost-effective and environmentally friendly.



#### 13.3c Case Study: Biodegradable Product Material Selection



In this subsection, we will further explore the case study of material selection for biodegradable products by focusing on the specific materials considered and their properties.



PLA is a biodegradable polymer made from renewable resources such as corn starch or sugar cane. It has gained popularity in recent years due to its biodegradability and mechanical properties, making it suitable for a wide range of applications. However, PLA does have some limitations, such as its relatively low heat resistance and brittleness.



PHA is another biodegradable polymer that is produced by microorganisms. It has similar properties to PLA, but with higher heat resistance and flexibility. However, PHA is currently more expensive to produce than PLA, making it less cost-effective for large-scale production.



PBAT is a biodegradable polyester that is commonly used in packaging materials. It has good mechanical properties and is relatively cost-effective. However, it is not as biodegradable as PLA or PHA, and its production process involves the use of non-renewable resources.



In conclusion, the case study showed that PLA was the optimal material for the biodegradable water bottle, considering all the criteria and sub-criteria. However, the selection of materials for biodegradable products should also take into account the specific application and its requirements. MADM methods provide a useful tool for evaluating and comparing materials, but ultimately, the decision should be based on a combination of technical, economic, and environmental factors.





### Section: 13.4 Case Study: Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products:



Biodegradable products have gained significant attention in recent years due to their potential to reduce environmental impact. However, the design of these products must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on the optimal design of biodegradable products using Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods.



#### 13.4a Introduction to Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products



The design of biodegradable products involves finding a balance between various objectives, such as cost, biodegradability, mechanical properties, and environmental impact. This can be a challenging task, as these objectives often conflict with each other. For example, using a more expensive biodegradable material may improve the product's environmental impact, but it may also increase the cost.



To address this challenge, MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different design options based on multiple criteria. These methods have been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In the following case study, we will use MADM methods to design a biodegradable product that meets multiple objectives.



#### 13.4b Application of MADM in Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products



To demonstrate the application of MADM in optimal design of biodegradable products, a case study was conducted to design a biodegradable water bottle. The design objectives for this product were identified as follows:



1. Minimize cost

2. Maximize biodegradability

3. Maximize mechanical strength

4. Minimize environmental impact



To evaluate different design options, a set of design variables were identified, including the type of biodegradable material, the thickness of the bottle, and the shape of the bottle. These design variables were then used to create a set of design alternatives.



Next, MADM methods were used to compare and evaluate these design alternatives based on the identified objectives. The Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP) was used to determine the relative importance of each objective, and the Technique for Order of Preference by Similarity to Ideal Solution (TOPSIS) was used to rank the design alternatives.



The results of the MADM analysis showed that a bottle made of polylactic acid (PLA) with a thickness of 2mm and a cylindrical shape was the optimal design option. This design option had the lowest cost, highest biodegradability, and highest mechanical strength compared to the other design alternatives.



#### 13.4c Conclusion



In this case study, we have demonstrated the application of MADM methods in the optimal design of biodegradable products. By using a systematic approach to evaluate design alternatives based on multiple criteria, we were able to identify the optimal design option that met the desired objectives. This approach can be applied to various other design problems in the field of biodegradable products, providing a comprehensive guide for designers and engineers.





### Section: 13.4 Case Study: Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products:



Biodegradable products have gained significant attention in recent years due to their potential to reduce environmental impact. However, the design of these products must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on the optimal design of biodegradable products using Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods.



#### 13.4a Introduction to Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products



The design of biodegradable products involves finding a balance between various objectives, such as cost, biodegradability, mechanical properties, and environmental impact. This can be a challenging task, as these objectives often conflict with each other. For example, using a more expensive biodegradable material may improve the product's environmental impact, but it may also increase the cost.



To address this challenge, MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different design options based on multiple criteria. These methods have been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In the following case study, we will use MADM methods to design a biodegradable product that meets multiple objectives.



#### 13.4b Application of MADM in Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products



To demonstrate the application of MADM in optimal design of biodegradable products, a case study was conducted to design a biodegradable water bottle. The design objectives for this product were identified as follows:



1. Minimize cost

2. Maximize biodegradability

3. Maximize mechanical strength

4. Minimize environmental impact



To evaluate different design options, a set of design variables were identified, including the type of biodegradable material, the thickness of the bottle, and the shape of the bottle. These design variables were then used to create a set of design alternatives.



To begin the MADM process, the first step was to establish a set of criteria for evaluating the design alternatives. These criteria were chosen based on the design objectives and included cost, biodegradability, mechanical strength, and environmental impact. Each criterion was assigned a weight based on its importance in the overall design.



Next, the design alternatives were evaluated using the chosen criteria. This involved collecting data on the cost, biodegradability, mechanical strength, and environmental impact of each design option. This data was then used to calculate a score for each alternative using a MADM method such as the Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP) or the Technique for Order of Preference by Similarity to Ideal Solution (TOPSIS).



After evaluating the design alternatives, the results showed that a bottle made of PLA (polylactic acid) with a thickness of 3mm and a cylindrical shape had the highest overall score. This design option had a low cost, high biodegradability, and good mechanical strength, making it the optimal choice for a biodegradable water bottle.



In conclusion, the application of MADM methods in the optimal design of biodegradable products can help designers make informed decisions that balance multiple objectives. By considering various design alternatives and evaluating them using a set of criteria, MADM methods can assist in creating sustainable and cost-effective biodegradable products. 





### Section: 13.4 Case Study: Optimal Design of Biodegradable Products:



Biodegradable products have gained significant attention in recent years due to their potential to reduce environmental impact. However, the design of these products must also be carefully considered to ensure optimal performance and cost-effectiveness. In this section, we will explore a case study on the optimal design of biodegradable products using Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) methods.



#### 13.4c Case Study: Biodegradable Product Design



In this case study, we will focus on the optimal design of a biodegradable water bottle. The design objectives for this product were identified as follows:



1. Minimize cost

2. Maximize biodegradability

3. Maximize mechanical strength

4. Minimize environmental impact



To achieve these objectives, we will use MADM methods to evaluate different design options and select the optimal design for the biodegradable water bottle.



#### 13.4c.1 Introduction to MADM Methods



MADM methods provide a systematic approach to compare and evaluate different design options based on multiple criteria. These methods have been successfully applied in various fields, including material selection and optimal design. In the case of biodegradable product design, MADM methods can help us find a balance between conflicting objectives, such as cost, biodegradability, mechanical strength, and environmental impact.



#### 13.4c.2 Identifying Design Variables and Alternatives



To evaluate different design options, a set of design variables were identified, including the type of biodegradable material, the thickness of the bottle, and the shape of the bottle. These design variables were then used to create a set of design alternatives. For example, the type of biodegradable material could be corn-based plastic, paper-based material, or biodegradable polymers.



#### 13.4c.3 Applying MADM Methods



To demonstrate the application of MADM in optimal design of biodegradable products, we will use the Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP) method. AHP is a popular MADM method that allows decision-makers to compare and prioritize alternatives based on a hierarchy of criteria. In this case, the criteria would be the design objectives, and the alternatives would be the different design options.



Using AHP, we can assign weights to each criterion based on its importance. For example, the weight for the cost criterion may be higher than the weight for the environmental impact criterion. Then, we can compare each design alternative against each criterion and assign a score based on its performance. Finally, we can calculate an overall score for each design alternative by multiplying the weight of each criterion by its corresponding score and summing them up.



#### 13.4c.4 Results and Discussion



After applying AHP to the design of the biodegradable water bottle, we found that the optimal design option was a bottle made of corn-based plastic with a medium thickness and a cylindrical shape. This design option scored the highest in terms of cost, biodegradability, and mechanical strength, while also having a relatively low environmental impact.



This case study demonstrates the effectiveness of MADM methods in finding a balance between conflicting objectives in the design of biodegradable products. By using a systematic approach, we can ensure that the final design meets the desired objectives and is optimized for performance and cost-effectiveness.

## Chapter: MADM with Applications in Material Selection and Optimal Design: A Comprehensive Guide



### Introduction



In the previous chapters, we have covered the fundamentals of Multiple Attribute Decision Making (MADM) and its applications in material selection and optimal design. We have explored various MADM methods such as the Analytic Hierarchy Process (AHP), Technique for Order of Preference by Similarity to Ideal Solution (TOPSIS), and the Preference Ranking Organization Method for Enrichment Evaluations (PROMETHEE). We have also discussed how these methods can be used to make decisions in material selection and optimal design problems.



In this chapter, we will delve deeper into the applications of MADM and optimal design. We will explore advanced topics and techniques that can be used to solve complex decision-making problems. These topics include sensitivity analysis, uncertainty analysis, and multi-objective optimization. We will also discuss how MADM can be integrated with other decision-making tools, such as Design of Experiments (DOE) and Finite Element Analysis (FEA), to enhance the decision-making process.



Furthermore, we will examine real-world case studies and examples to demonstrate the practical applications of MADM and optimal design. These case studies will cover a wide range of industries, including aerospace, automotive, and consumer products. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of how MADM and optimal design can be applied in various industries and decision-making scenarios.



In summary, this chapter aims to provide readers with a deeper understanding of MADM and optimal design and how they can be used to make informed decisions in complex decision-making problems. It will serve as a valuable resource for engineers, researchers, and students who are interested in utilizing MADM and optimal design in their work. 





### Section: 14.1 Application in Healthcare Industry:



The healthcare industry has been greatly impacted by the emergence of digital twin technology. This technology has the potential to revolutionize the way healthcare is delivered by providing personalized and data-driven solutions for patients. In this section, we will explore how MADM and optimal design can be applied in the healthcare industry to improve patient outcomes and enhance the overall healthcare system.



#### 14.1a Introduction to MADM and Optimal Design in Healthcare



The concept of digital twin in the healthcare industry was first introduced in product or equipment prognostics. However, with advancements in technology, it is now possible to create personalized models for patients based on their health and lifestyle parameters. These models can be continuously adjusted to track changes in the patient's health and provide tailored solutions for their specific needs.



One of the key applications of MADM in healthcare is in the selection of materials for medical devices and equipment. The use of appropriate materials is crucial in ensuring the safety and effectiveness of medical devices. MADM methods such as AHP and TOPSIS can be used to evaluate and compare different materials based on multiple attributes such as biocompatibility, durability, and cost. This can help healthcare professionals make informed decisions when selecting materials for medical devices.



Moreover, optimal design techniques can be applied in the development of medical devices to improve their performance and functionality. By using techniques such as Design of Experiments (DOE) and Finite Element Analysis (FEA), engineers can optimize the design of medical devices to meet specific requirements and constraints. This can lead to the development of more efficient and reliable medical devices, ultimately improving patient outcomes.



In addition to material selection and optimal design, MADM and optimal design can also be applied in healthcare for decision-making in treatment plans. By considering multiple attributes such as effectiveness, cost, and patient preferences, MADM methods can assist healthcare professionals in making decisions that are tailored to the individual patient's needs. This can lead to more personalized and effective treatment plans, ultimately improving patient satisfaction and outcomes.



Furthermore, the integration of MADM and optimal design with other decision-making tools, such as digital twin technology, can further enhance the decision-making process in healthcare. By combining these tools, healthcare professionals can have a more comprehensive understanding of the patient's health and make more informed decisions.



In conclusion, the application of MADM and optimal design in the healthcare industry has the potential to greatly improve patient outcomes and enhance the overall healthcare system. By utilizing these methods, healthcare professionals can make data-driven and personalized decisions that can lead to better patient care.

#### 14.1b Application of MADM and Optimal Design in Healthcare

This can help healthcare professionals make informed decisions when selecting materials for medical devices.
